<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><img alt="Silver medal – second place" data-file-height="16" data-file-width="16" height="16" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/16px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/24px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg/32px-Silver_medal_icon_%28S_initial%29.svg.png 2x" title="Silver medal – second place" width="16"/></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/1990_Goodwill_Games" title="1990 Goodwill Games">1990 Seattle</a></span></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle;">Team competition</td>
</tr>
</table>
</div>
</div>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Alonzo Harding Mourning, Jr.</b> (born February 8, 1970) is an American retired professional <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a> player, who played most of his 15-year <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">National Basketball Association</a> (NBA) career for the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Heat" title="Miami Heat">Miami Heat</a>.</p>
<p>Nicknamed "<b>Zo</b>", Mourning played at <a href="/wiki/Center_(basketball)" title="Center (basketball)">center</a>. Following his college basketball career at <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a>, his tenacity on defense twice earned him <a href="/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award">NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award</a> and perennially placed him on the <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Defensive_Team" title="NBA All-Defensive Team">NBA All-Defensive Team</a>. Mourning made a comeback after undergoing a kidney transplant and later won the 2006 NBA Championship with the Heat. Mourning also played for the <a href="/wiki/Charlotte_Hornets" title="Charlotte Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/New_Jersey_Nets" title="New Jersey Nets">New Jersey Nets</a>. On March 30, 2009, Mourning became the first <a href="/wiki/Miami_Heat" title="Miami Heat">Miami Heat</a> player to have his number retired.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup> Since June 26, 2009, Mourning has served as Vice President of Player Programs and Development for the Heat. On August 8, 2014, Mourning was inducted into the <a href="/wiki/Naismith_Memorial_Basketball_Hall_of_Fame" title="Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame">Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Basketball_career">Basketball career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Basketball career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During his time at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_River_High_School_(Virginia)" title="Indian River High School (Virginia)">Indian River High School</a> in Chesapeake, Virginia, he led the team to 51 straight victories and a state title his junior year (1987). As a senior he averaged 25 points, 15 rebounds and 12 blocked shots a game. He was named Player of the Year by USA Today, Parade, Gatorade, and Naismith. Mourning played <a href="/wiki/College_basketball" title="College basketball">college basketball</a> for the <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">Georgetown University</a> <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_Hoyas" title="Georgetown Hoyas">Hoyas</a>. He led the nation in blocked shots his freshman year and was an All-American his last year there.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Charlotte_Hornets">Charlotte Hornets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Charlotte Hornets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_unsourced" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><img alt="" data-file-height="40" data-file-width="40" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" width="40"/></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section of a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Biographies_of_living_persons" title="Wikipedia:Biographies of living persons">biography of a living person</a> <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">include</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">references or sources</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Please help by adding <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">reliable sources</a>. Contentious material about living people that is unsourced or poorly sourced <b>must be removed immediately</b>.<br/>
<small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22&amp;num=50" rel="nofollow">"Alonzo Mourning"</a> – <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22&amp;tbm=nws" rel="nofollow">news</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers" rel="nofollow">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22" rel="nofollow">books</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22" rel="nofollow">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="http://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on" rel="nofollow">JSTOR</a> <b>·</b> <a class="external text" href="//www.google.com/images?safe=off&amp;tbm=isch&amp;tbs=sur:fmc&amp;q=%22Alonzo+Mourning%22+-site:wikipedia.org+-site:wikimedia.org" rel="nofollow">free images</a></span></small></span> <small><i>(June 2014)</i></small> <small class="hide-when-compact"><i>(<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Mourning was selected second overall in the <a href="/wiki/1992_NBA_draft" title="1992 NBA draft">1992 NBA draft</a> by the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Charlotte_Hornets_season" title="1992–93 Charlotte Hornets season">Charlotte Hornets</a>, behind <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O'Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> Mourning was named to the league's all-rookie team in 1993 after averaging 21.0 pts, 10.3 rebounds, and 3.47 blocks. He finished second to Shaquille O'Neal in rookie of the year voting.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4"><a href="#cite_note-4">[4]</a></sup> He posted the highest scoring average of any rookie in Hornets history. Mourning and O'Neal were the first NBA rookies since <a href="/wiki/David_Robinson_(basketball)" title="David Robinson (basketball)">David Robinson</a> in <a href="/wiki/1989%E2%80%9390_NBA_season" title="1989–90 NBA season">1989–90</a> to average 20 or more points and 10-plus rebounds in their first seasons. Mourning shattered Charlotte's blocked-shots records, becoming the Hornets' all-time career leader in the 49th game of the season. The greatest moment of Mourning's rookie season came on May 5, 1993 in Game 4 of a first-round playoff series against the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_Boston_Celtics_season" title="1992–93 Boston Celtics season">Boston Celtics</a>. His 20-footer at the buzzer gave the Hornets a 104–103 victory in the game and a three-games-to-one victory in the series. The Hornets lost in the second round to the <a href="/wiki/1992%E2%80%9393_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1992–93 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a> in 5 games, with Mourning averaging of 23.8 points, 9.9 rebounds and 3.4 blocks in 9 playoff games. The following year, Mourning played in just 60 games, maintaining similar averages<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (June 2014)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup> in points, rebounds and blocks, but the Hornets missed the playoffs.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_NBA_season" title="1994–95 NBA season">1994–95 season</a>, Mourning and teammate <a href="/wiki/Larry_Johnson_(basketball,_born_1969)" title="Larry Johnson (basketball, born 1969)">Larry Johnson</a> led the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Charlotte_Hornets_season" title="1994–95 Charlotte Hornets season">Hornets</a> to a 50-win season and reached the playoffs. Mourning ranked first on the team in <a href="/wiki/Point_(basketball)" title="Point (basketball)">scoring</a> (21.3 ppg), <a href="/wiki/Rebound_(basketball)" title="Rebound (basketball)">rebounding</a> (9.9 rpg), <a href="/wiki/Block_(basketball)" title="Block (basketball)">blocked shots</a> (2.92 per game), and <a href="/wiki/Field_goal_percentage" title="Field goal percentage">field goal percentage</a> (.519), and played in the <a href="/wiki/1995_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="1995 NBA All-Star Game">1995 NBA All-Star Game</a> where he scored 10 points and grabbed 8 rebounds. The Hornets lost in 4 games to the <a href="/wiki/1994%E2%80%9395_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="1994–95 Chicago Bulls season">Chicago Bulls</a> in the first round of the playoffs, despite Mourning posting 22 points, 13.3 rebounds and 3.3 blocks for the series.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Miami_Heat">Miami Heat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Miami Heat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On November 3, 1995, after Mourning rejected a contract extension offer worth an average of $11.2 million for seven years, the Hornets traded him, along with reserves <a href="/wiki/Pete_Myers" title="Pete Myers">Pete Myers</a> and <a href="/wiki/LeRon_Ellis" title="LeRon Ellis">LeRon Ellis</a> in exchange for <a href="/wiki/Glen_Rice" title="Glen Rice">Glen Rice</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Geiger" title="Matt Geiger">Matt Geiger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Khalid_Reeves" title="Khalid Reeves">Khalid Reeves</a> and a first-round pick in the <a href="/wiki/1996_NBA_draft" title="1996 NBA draft">1996 NBA draft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mourning served as the centerpiece of the <a href="/wiki/Pat_Riley" title="Pat Riley">Pat Riley</a>-coached Heat, and in his first season with the team he averaged 23.2 points, 10.4 rebounds and 2.7 blocks a game as Miami made the playoffs before being swept in the first round by the 72 win <a href="/wiki/1995%E2%80%9396_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="1995–96 Chicago Bulls season">Chicago Bulls</a>. Mourning played in the <a href="/wiki/1996_NBA_All-Star_Game" title="1996 NBA All-Star Game">1996 NBA All-Star Game</a> and was joined by all-star point guard <a href="/wiki/Tim_Hardaway" title="Tim Hardaway">Tim Hardaway</a> who arrived through a midseason trade.</p>
<p>The following year, the Heat won a franchise record 61 wins, second in the Eastern Conference to the defending champion Bulls, and Mourning averaged 19.8 points, 9.9 rebounds and 2.9 blocks. In the playoffs, Miami defeated the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Orlando_Magic_season" title="1996–97 Orlando Magic season">Orlando Magic</a> in five games, and advanced to the conference semifinals against the <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1996–97 New York Knicks season">New York Knicks</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Heat%E2%80%93Knicks_rivalry" title="Heat–Knicks rivalry">the rivalry</a> between the Heat and the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Knicks" title="New York Knicks">New York Knicks</a> intensified. The Knicks took a 3-1 lead in the series, but following a brawl between him and <a href="/wiki/Charles_Oakley" title="Charles Oakley">Charles Oakley</a>, late in Game 5, in which multiple suspensions were handed down, Mourning scored 28 points in Game 6 followed by a 22-point, 12-rebound performance in Game 7 to help Miami advanced to the Eastern Conference Finals, a franchise first, to face Chicago. The <a href="/wiki/1996%E2%80%9397_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="1996–97 Chicago Bulls season">Bulls</a> took a 3-0 lead in the series, and Mourning guaranteed a victory in Game 4.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> The Heat won the Game 87–80 but still lost the series in five games.</p>
<p>The next season, Mourning posted similar averages but only played in 58 games, and Miami was eliminated in the first round by the <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1997–98 New York Knicks season">Knicks</a>, a series in which Mourning was suspended for the 5th and deciding game due to an on-court fight with ex-teammate <a href="/wiki/Larry_Johnson_(basketball,_born_1969)" title="Larry Johnson (basketball, born 1969)">Larry Johnson</a>, with Knicks Head Coach <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Van_Gundy" title="Jeff Van Gundy">Jeff Van Gundy</a> hanging onto Mourning's leg in an attempt to break it up.</p>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_NBA_lockout" title="1998–99 NBA lockout">lockout-shortened</a> 1998–1999 season, Mourning averaged 20.1 points, a career high 11 rebounds and a career high 3.9 blocks per game as Miami won another Atlantic Division title and the top seed in the playoffs. Mourning won the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Defensive_Player_of_the_Year_Award" title="NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award">NBA Defensive Player of the Year Award</a>, was named <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/All-NBA_First_Team" title="All-NBA First Team">All-NBA First Team</a> and finished second to <a href="/wiki/Karl_Malone" title="Karl Malone">Karl Malone</a> in the <a href="/wiki/NBA_Most_Valuable_Player_Award" title="NBA Most Valuable Player Award">NBA Most Valuable Player Award</a> voting. Despite being the top seed, the Heat lost to the eighth-seeded <a href="/wiki/1998%E2%80%9399_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1998–99 New York Knicks season">Knicks</a> in five games, off a last-second shot by <a href="/wiki/Allan_Houston" title="Allan Houston">Allan Houston</a> in Miami.</p>
<p>The following season, Mourning averaged 21.7 points a game, 9.5 rebounds and 3.7 blocks a game, and won his second straight Defensive Player of the Year Award. Miami swept the <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="1999–2000 Detroit Pistons season">Detroit Pistons</a> in the first round of the playoffs, with Mourning dominating the Pistons<sup class="noprint Inline-Template noprint Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="This term requires quantification. (June 2014)">quantify</span></a></i>]</sup>. The Heat faced <a href="/wiki/1999%E2%80%932000_New_York_Knicks_season" title="1999–2000 New York Knicks season">New York</a>, the fourth straight year that the two teams met in the postseason, and took a 3-2 series lead, but New York won the series in seven games. In the summer, Mourning and Hardaway won a gold medal with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="United States men's national basketball team">United States</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics_%E2%80%93_Men%27s_tournament" title="Basketball at the 2000 Summer Olympics – Men's tournament">Olympics in Sydney</a>.</p>
<p>During the offseason, Miami underwent an overhaul and expectations leading up to the season were high.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Prior the start of the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_NBA_season" title="2000–01 NBA season">2000–01 season</a>, however, Mourning was diagnosed with <a href="/wiki/Focal_segmental_glomerulosclerosis" title="Focal segmental glomerulosclerosis">focal segmental glomerulosclerosis</a>, a kidney condition, that caused him to miss the first five months of the season. He returned to play on March 27, and played a total of 13 games as Miami made the postseason but were swept in the first round by the <a href="/wiki/2000%E2%80%9301_Charlotte_Hornets_season" title="2000–01 Charlotte Hornets season">Charlotte Hornets</a>.</p>
<p>The following year, Mourning played in 75 games despite his kidney disease, and was selected to play in the 2002 <a href="/wiki/NBA_All-Star_Game" title="NBA All-Star Game">NBA All-Star Game</a>, where he scored 13 points off the bench. He averaged 15.7 points, 8.4 rebounds and 2.5 blocks a game, but the Heat missed the playoffs. As his condition worsened, Mourning did not play during the entire <a href="/wiki/2002%E2%80%9303_NBA_season" title="2002–03 NBA season">2002–03 season</a> and his expiring contract was not renewed by the Heat.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Jersey_Nets">New Jersey Nets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: New Jersey Nets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Mourning signed a four-year deal with the <a href="/wiki/2003%E2%80%9304_New_Jersey_Nets_season" title="2003–04 New Jersey Nets season">New Jersey Nets</a> in 2003 as a free agent. But on November 25, 2003, Mourning retired from the NBA due to complications from his kidney disease. On December 19 of that year he underwent a successful kidney transplant. In 2004 he started practicing with the Nets again, and made the team's regular season roster during the 2004–05 season. He did not play a significant role with the Nets, however, and openly complained to the media that he wanted out of New Jersey, especially after the team traded away <a href="/wiki/Kenyon_Martin" title="Kenyon Martin">Kenyon Martin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> Mourning was traded to the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Toronto_Raptors_season" title="2004–05 Toronto Raptors season">Toronto Raptors</a> on December 17, 2004. Mourning never reported to the Raptors, and was bought out of his contract at a remaining 9 million dollars on February 11, 2005. Raptors team officials later said that he did not meet the medical conditions to play for the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup> Mourning then finished the season with the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Miami_Heat_season" title="2004–05 Miami Heat season">Miami Heat</a> being paid a second salary, the veteran's minimum.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Return_to_Miami_Heat">Return to Miami Heat</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Return to Miami Heat">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After being unhappy at the prospect of playing for a losing franchise,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Mourning re-signed with the Heat on March 1, 2005. His role was reduced as a backup because of superstar <a href="/wiki/Shaquille_O%27Neal" title="Shaquille O'Neal">Shaquille O'Neal</a>, although he was called upon as a starter due to O'Neal missing stretches due to injury. O'Neal and Mourning even played together on the court at times, with Mourning playing power forward. Because of physical limitations, his minutes were reduced, but was still a steady contributor. Mourning's tenacious defense, steady offense, and all around hustle helped the Heat gain and maintain the second-best record in the NBA's Eastern conference during the 2004–05 season. Mourning finished the regular season ranking third in blocked shots at 2.66 per game, despite only playing 20 minutes per contest. Miami swept the Nets in the first round of the playoffs, with Mourning scoring 21 points with 9 rebounds in just 16 minutes in game 2. In the second round against the <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Washington_Wizards_season" title="2004–05 Washington Wizards season">Washington Wizards</a>, Mourning stepped in for the injured O'Neal and scored 14 points with 13 rebounds and 4 blocked shots in game 3 as Miami completed another four game sweep. Miami fell in seven games to the defending champion <a href="/wiki/2004%E2%80%9305_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="2004–05 Detroit Pistons season">Detroit Pistons</a> in the Eastern Conference Finals, with Mourning leading the team in blocks with 3 per game for the series.</p>
<p>Mourning re-signed with Miami, as the Heat once again re-hauled their roster, acquiring other veterans seeking a title such as <a href="/wiki/Antoine_Walker" title="Antoine Walker">Antoine Walker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gary_Payton" title="Gary Payton">Gary Payton</a>. Mourning continued to serve as the Heat's backup center, and early on stepped in to serve as the team's starting center after O'Neal suffered an injury early on. Mourning started in 20 games out of a total of 65 games played, averaging 7.8 points and 5.5 rebounds while finishing third in the league with 2.7 blocks a game despite playing as a reserve. In the playoffs, Mourning continued to shine in his role as a defensive player off the bench, as Miami advanced past the <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Chicago_Bulls_season" title="2005–06 Chicago Bulls season">Chicago Bulls</a> and New Jersey before defeating <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Detroit_Pistons_season" title="2005–06 Detroit Pistons season">Detroit</a> in 6 games to advance to the <a href="/wiki/2006_NBA_Finals" title="2006 NBA Finals">2006 NBA Finals</a>, the first NBA Finals in franchise history and the first for Mourning. After a 2-0 deficit, Miami won all three of its home games led by the spectacular play of <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a>, and in game 6 in <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_Dallas_Mavericks_season" title="2005–06 Dallas Mavericks season">Dallas</a> Mourning came off the bench to score 8 points with 6 rebounds and a team high 5 blocks to help Miami win its first NBA Championship in franchise history.</p>
<p>After winning the championship, Mourning announced that he would return to the Heat in <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_NBA_season" title="2006–07 NBA season">2006–07</a> to defend their title, despite receiving offers of more money from other teams, including the <a href="/wiki/2006%E2%80%9307_San_Antonio_Spurs_season" title="2006–07 San Antonio Spurs season">San Antonio Spurs</a>. In 2007, Mourning announced he would return for one more year with the Heat and his 15th season. "It will definitely be my last year", Mourning said. After starting the season on a solid note averaging 6 points, 3.8 rebounds and 1.75 blocks in just over 16 minutes played per 24 games,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Mourning tore his <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patellar_tendon" title="Patellar tendon">patellar tendon</a> in his right knee<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> on December 19, 2007, during the first quarter of a loss in <a href="/wiki/2007%E2%80%9308_Atlanta_Hawks_season" title="2007–08 Atlanta Hawks season">Atlanta</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> The injury, which occurred on the fourth anniversary of his successful kidney transplant, was said<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (February 2009)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> to be career-threatening, but rumors persisted<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (February 2009)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> about a return come the 2008–09 season, and Mourning himself said that this was not the way he wanted to end his career considering all he had been through already.</p>
<p>Mourning has averaged the most blocks in the NBA per 48 minutes with 5.46.</p>
<p>During the 2007–08 season, he became the Heat's all-time leader in points scored (which has since been surpassed by <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a>).</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Retirement">Retirement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Retirement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mourning announced his retirement from the NBA on January 22, 2009. In his press conference he said, "I'm 38 years old and I feel like I have physically done all I can for this game."<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> One month later, the Heat announced that they would retire Mourning's number 33 jersey, making him the first Heat player to be so honored.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The jersey retirement ceremony occurred on March 30, 2009, when the Heat hosted the Orlando Magic. During the extended halftime ceremony, Mourning was introduced by Florida Governor <a href="/wiki/Charlie_Crist" title="Charlie Crist">Charlie Crist</a>; former Georgetown University basketball coach <a href="/wiki/John_Thompson_(basketball)" title="John Thompson (basketball)">John Thompson</a>; Basketball Hall of Famer <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a>; Heat players <a href="/wiki/Dwyane_Wade" title="Dwyane Wade">Dwyane Wade</a> and <a href="/wiki/Udonis_Haslem" title="Udonis Haslem">Udonis Haslem</a>; and Heat head coach <a href="/wiki/Pat_Riley" title="Pat Riley">Pat Riley</a>.</p>
<p>In May 2009 he was named to the Hampton Roads Sports Hall of Fame, which honors athletes, coaches and administrators who contributed to sports in southeastern Virginia. In the following April, he was inducted into the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Virginia_Sports_Hall_of_Fame" title="Virginia Sports Hall of Fame">Virginia Sports Hall of Fame</a> in recognition of his outstanding high school, collegiate, and professional career as well as his commitment to volunteer service in the communities in which he has lived and worked throughout his life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Mourning announced his return to the Heat in late June 2009; he holds the position of Vice President of Player Programs and Development, which covers community outreach and mentoring young players.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> On July 2014 the NBA announced that Mourning would be inducted into the Naismith Memorial Basketball Hall of Fame on August 8.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Career_highlights">Career highlights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Career highlights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li><b>NBA champion</b>: 2006 (as a player), 2012, 2013 (as vice president of player programs)</li>
<li><b>All-NBA First Team</b>: 1999</li>
<li><b>All-NBA Second Team</b>: 2000</li>
<li><b>2-time NBA Defensive Player of the Year</b>: 1999, 2000</li>
<li><b>2-time NBA All-Defensive First Team</b>: 1999, 2000</li>
<li><b>7-time NBA All-Star</b>: 1994, 1995, 1996, 1997, 2000, 2001, 2002</li>
<li>Heat franchise second leading scorer with 9,459 points</li>
<li>Led NBA in blocked shots: 3.91 bpg in 1999</li>
<li>NBA All-Rookie 1st Team in 1993</li>
<li>Won bronze at the <a href="/wiki/1990_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1990 FIBA World Championship">1990 FIBA World Championship</a> with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="United States men's national basketball team">US national team</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></li>
<li>Won gold at the <a href="/wiki/1994_FIBA_World_Championship" title="1994 FIBA World Championship">1994 FIBA World Championship</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Basketball_at_the_2000_Summer_Olympics" title="Basketball at the 2000 Summer Olympics">2000 Olympic Games</a> with the <a href="/wiki/United_States_men%27s_national_basketball_team" title="United States men's national basketball team">US national team</a></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Kidney_transplant">Kidney transplant</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Kidney transplant">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>On November 25, 2003, Mourning's cousin and a retired <a href="/wiki/United_States_Marine_Corps" title="United States Marine Corps">U. S. Marine</a>, Jason Cooper, was visiting Mourning's gravely ill grandmother in the hospital. Mourning's father was present and informed Cooper that Mourning was retiring that very same day from the NBA because of a life-threatening kidney disease, <a href="/wiki/Focal_segmental_glomerulosclerosis" title="Focal segmental glomerulosclerosis">focal segmental glomerulosclerosis</a>, the same problem that <a href="/wiki/Sean_Elliott" title="Sean Elliott">Sean Elliott</a> had in 1999. Cooper asked if there was anything he could do, and began to contemplate donating one of his kidneys to his estranged cousin, whom he had not seen in 25 years and whom he only knew through basketball. Cooper was tested for compatibility, along with many other family members and friends (including fellow NBA center and good friend <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Ewing" title="Patrick Ewing">Patrick Ewing</a>); during his grandmother's funeral, Mourning received the news that Jason Cooper was a match.</p>
<p>Mourning received Cooper's left kidney on December 19, 2003.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LVA_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-LVA-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Charitable_work">Charitable work</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Charitable work">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="750" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg/220px-Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg/330px-Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2f/Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg/440px-Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bill_Clinton_Alonzo_Mourning_CGI_U.jpeg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Alonzo Mourning with former U.S. President <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">Bill Clinton</a> during <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Clinton_Global_Initiative" title="Clinton Global Initiative">Clinton Global Initiative</a> University Day of Service at <a href="/wiki/Carrfour_Supportive_Housing" title="Carrfour Supportive Housing">Carrfour Supportive Housing</a> community for formerly homeless families in <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami</a>, Florida.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1997, Mourning established Alonzo Mourning Charities Inc. to aid in the development of children and families living in at-risk situations and provides support and services that enhance the lives of youth of promise.</p>
<p>After being diagnosed with focal <a href="/wiki/Glomerulosclerosis" title="Glomerulosclerosis">glomerulosclerosis</a> (FSGS), Mourning launched Zo's Fund for Life, a campaign which seeks to raise funds for research, education, and testing to fight focal glomerulosclerosis. Funds are allocated toward research for a cure, education for doctors and the general public, testing for early detection and a fund for those not able to afford medication.</p>
<p>In 2007, Mourning along with <a href="/wiki/Andre_Agassi" title="Andre Agassi">Andre Agassi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_Ali" title="Muhammad Ali">Muhammad Ali</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lance_Armstrong" title="Lance Armstrong">Lance Armstrong</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warrick_Dunn" title="Warrick Dunn">Warrick Dunn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mia_Hamm" title="Mia Hamm">Mia Hamm</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Gordon" title="Jeff Gordon">Jeff Gordon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tony_Hawk" title="Tony Hawk">Tony Hawk</a>, <a href="/wiki/Andrea_Jaeger" title="Andrea Jaeger">Andrea Jaeger</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Joyner-Kersee" title="Jackie Joyner-Kersee">Jackie Joyner-Kersee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mario_Lemieux" title="Mario Lemieux">Mario Lemieux</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cal_Ripken,_Jr." title="Cal Ripken, Jr.">Cal Ripken, Jr.</a> founded <a href="/wiki/Athletes_for_Hope" title="Athletes for Hope">Athletes for Hope</a>, a charitable organization, which helps professional athletes get involved in charitable causes and inspires millions of non-athletes to volunteer and support the community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2003 he also founded the Overtown Youth Center for underprivileged kids, located in Miami, Florida. The program aims to inspire, empower, and enrich these children while teaching them to become positive contributing citizens.</p>
<p>In 2009, the <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County_Public_Schools" title="Miami-Dade County Public Schools">Miami-Dade school board</a> named a new high school in <a href="/wiki/North_Miami,_Florida" title="North Miami, Florida">North Miami, Florida</a> in his honor, <a href="/wiki/Alonzo_and_Tracy_Mourning_Senior_High_Biscayne_Bay_Campus" title="Alonzo and Tracy Mourning Senior High Biscayne Bay Campus">Alonzo and Tracy Mourning Senior High Biscayne Bay Campus</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Alonzo_Mourning&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Mourning and his wife Tracy have three children: a son named Alonzo III ("Trey"), a daughter named Myka Sydney, and a second son named Alijah (born September 18, 2009).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> They reside in <a href="/wiki/Pinecrest,_Florida" title="Pinecrest, Florida">Pinecrest, Florida</a>, where Mourning purchased a two-story, 9,786-square-foot residence for $4.5 million in 2012.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p>
<p>In July 2011 Mourning was sued by Miami-based lawyer Spencer Aronfeld on behalf of Alberto Candoleria for crashing his car into another car and then leaving the scene of the accident. The Florida Highway Patrol later charged Mourning with leaving the scene of a car accident. The accident allegedly occurred after he left <a href="/wiki/Chris_Bosh" title="Chris Bosh">Chris Bosh</a>'s wedding in Miami Beach after 3:00 A.M. Candoleria had just been in an accident when Mourning struck his car. He did not know if he was in his car when Mourning hit him as he claimed to have amnesia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015 Mourning was one of eight Virginians honored in the <a href="/wiki/Library_of_Virginia" title="Library of Virginia">Library of Virginia</a>'s "Strong Men &amp; Women in Virginia History" for his charitable work and for his contributions to the sport of basketball.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-LVA_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-LVA-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
